The reason it likely froze like it did is because the zeds, being as fast as they were, in such large numbers, and being able to place AND break blocks at the speed they move, likely placed and/or removed more blocks than the game, or even your pc, was able to handle in such a short time. Because it ONLY happened when you went into the middle, where there were thousands of blocks that the zeds, which had completely surrounded your base, could break. Meaning hundreds of zombies, at once, were placing and/or breaking blocks all at once, causing the game to basically freeze as it was updating THOUSANDS of blocks at once. And old versions of Minecraft are NOTORIOUS for not being able to handle that many block updates at once.  I particularly remember, on the old Xbox version of the game, just placing slab platforms a few dozen blocks in the air would cause lag spikes, because it was updating the light levels from the slabs all the way down to and below the ground. It was BAD. And now imagine blocks are being REMOVED at a much higher rate. It's not going to go well for the game.

Your spawn points and your only hope for oxygen and surface items are boats, submarines, underground bases, and caves. The deeper you go, the darker it gets and the more you become dependent on light sources. You can craft scuba gear, oxygen tanks, flashlights, flippers, and diving suits. Mobs to encounter would be sharks, fish, dolphins, squids, angler fish, crabs, krakens, and even megalodons. 3. Mythological monsters: A majority of mobs will either attempt to kill you or assist you (mostly kill). In addition to the well-known monsters such as cyclopes, sphinxes, vampires, werewolves, centaurs, satyrs, faeries, and dragons, there are also lesser known monsters such as girtablilu (scorpion centaurs), Nuckalevee, amphisbaena, and wendigoes.  please like so forge labs can see this and reply which one's your favorite.

some things that might help with the growing issue would be to put more torches by the potatoes, since it produces more light, and also checking if you have a simulation distance setting and if you do turn it up. Simulation distance is how many chunks around you are interacting, so if your potatoes are outside of your simulation distance, they won't grow.  Edit: Also, rotten flesh is something you can eat. it will give you hunger for about 30 seconds, but if you stay still it shouldn't do too much.

FORGE YOU GOTTA READ THIS BRO  The reason your crops didn't grow is probably because the game tick speed is set to ZERO!  It's the same reason why your leaves never decayed, and your fire never went out! When the game's tick speed is zero, ticks don't activate. This means crops wont grow, fire wont spread or go out, leaves won't decay, and a lot of other things as well based on random ticks!

I found the issue with your slabs! You placed them on the point where a normal block would be, so instead of a half block (a no-spawning section) you essentially just made a wooden floor, which allows spawning. (Or at least that is what I believe occurred).
Hi Sean! Just started watching your videos this week and I think they're great!  A little tip or two, if I may. -Your infinite water source only needs to be three blocks in a line with a bucket dumped in each end. Take from the middle.  -Plant crops in 9x9 squares with one bit of water in the center. Cover the water with a log, torch on top.  -Mob farms work best when way up high, over a body of water. The game will localise the spawning to your setup rather than the surrounding caves etc.  I hope those are helpful! Thanks for the laughs and thrills! R.L. Craft was intense!

My man Sean you straight up forgot you had 15 blocks of hay 9:06 that would be so much wheat
about the crops: I believe you got the random tick speed set to 0 (which would explain why the fire you put on the bottom of the hole didn't went out, normally fire only stays on when its on top of netherrack), in order to fix it you gotta run the command "/gamerule randomtickspeed 3" which will set it to its default state, if you increase or decrease the number the random tick speed will be increased or decreased which has an effect on pretty much anything that has random timings. Also note that if you increase it to much the game will lag massively.

Hey Sean, mobs should be unable to spawn on slabs, so if you need to make a place mob free without torches, just build a floor of slabs. Also mobs will walk over trapdoors as if they were a block, even if they were open and there's a drop right under it. So if you need to make a trap just put a trapdoor on the floor and open it. Tip for making Obsidian. Don't put the water the same block you put the lava. The source block of the lava makes the obsidian while the flowing lava makes the cobblestone, so putting the water on the block the source block is will make it disappear.

And while I'm sure someone else in the comments has answered this question for you, but to make obsidian you need to place the lava first and then place the water on a block above and to the side of the lava so the water can stream down to it. It will then turn to obsidian. If the lava stream and water stream meet, it will just make cobblestone (which is a good way to get infinite cobblestone) but the lava source getting water on it directly will turn it to stone unless it's the water stream.

TIPS!  Make sure your slabs are on the BOTTOM. If slabs are on the TOP of a block(the top half of a normal block), they can still spawn mobs!  A way you can test without going to the edge is to place water! If it empties and you can see the water, you did it right! If it disappears, you made a waterlogged slab and the water is under it!  Also, you need to place the boat down and get the villager to walk into it(as long as the mod pack doesn't disable this).  Another way to mobproof is to spam buttons everywhere. They won't look the best, but they're cheap. Especially if you use stone.

I have two mod ideas for you: 1) Food and Ore is swapped. You have to mine "ore" blocks to get food, and grow crops when then will drop ore instead of food (crops will still drop seeds so you can keep growing them... maybe...) 2) The world is marbled in extreme biome zones. You have veins of safety, but there's no resources there. you have to adventure into one of the extremes. Either the zone is hot or cold, and the closer you get to the center of one of these zones, the greater the temperature difference, with the exact center being these invisble one block pillars that are enough to instakill via heat or cold if you stand in them. Also, the closer you get to the center of one of these zones, the better the resources you'll find. - if you do one or both of these for a 100 day survival, then I have another idea. Set it up so every 25 days, you unlock two additional mods, one that you select that will help you, and your friend will select a mod without telling you what it is, that will hinder you. Like day 50 you gain access to a mod that gives you better armor, but on the downside, you now deal with dinosaurs trying to eat you. The idea is that for these three sets of unlockable mods, they get better (or worse) the longer you survive.

The reason that your crops weren't growing is that crops only grow when the chunk is loaded.  If you're spending your time away from that chunk, everything in that chunk unloads and freezes in time.   Crops only progress while you're in the same area as them.  It's not a problem with the mod.  This is how Minecraft works.

Time to talk about spawning mechanics!  Yes, light level is good, but mobs canâ€™t spawn on anything but a full block. That means that stairs, slabs, glass, etc are great lightless ways of spawn-proofing areas. However, itâ€™d have to be every single block.  Also, you might want to try using pathfinding mechanics to your advantage. Mobs consider buttons and trapdoors as something they can walk on, even if the trapdoor is open, allowing them to fall.  Minecraft can be weird sometimes.
With the cropsâ€¦I think the tick speed for the map was set to zero which was why any fire you lit never went out. Crops grow at random tick speeds so if set to zero they will never grow. If u encounter issues like that in the future message the person who built the map so they can check the settings. Also you HAVE to stay where the chuck your crops are in stays loaded for them to grow. So if chunk distance is set at say 16 chunks then you canâ€™t go more than 15 chunks away if you want the crops to grow. And crops should be fully grown within 1-4 days after planting. Itâ€™s not exact bc they grow randomly based on tick speed. The lower the tick speed the slower they grow & the higher the tick speed the faster they grow. You can easily check to get a rough idea of what the tick speed is set to by making a line of wooden blocks and set the first on fire and see how quickly the fire spreads to the next plank OR light several fires on block that donâ€™t burn and see how long it lasts. Normally it should only burn for 15-20 seconds at most.  â€” Another option for forcing crops to growâ€¦ if bonemeal works & composters are in the version you are playing in then u can get bonemeal from using shears on leaves & other plants and putting it in a composter. Itâ€™s not super efficient but could save you in a pinch.

If you don't want stuff spawning somewhere you can also use buttons or carpet. As mobs can't spawn on those blocks. and Zombies won't walk on blocks that have carpet on them I think. Your crops won't grow because you are out of render distance which is when you are so far away that they unload and get frozen in time until loaded back in. So you need to stay by your crops for them to load. or it is because every place you go it's winter or Antarctica so that may also be the reason why.
